Here is the list of complex words provided as plain text for easy copying and pasting:Advanced Vocabulary (Complex Meanings)Ephemeral /蓹藞f蓻m蓹r蓹l/ (adj.): Lasting for a very short time. Example: The beauty of a sunset is ephemeral.Obfuscate /藞蓲bf蕦ske瑟t/ (verb): To make something unclear, obscure, or unintelligible. Example: The politician tried to obfuscate the issue.Serendipity /藢s蓻r蓹n藞d瑟p瑟ti/ (noun): Finding valuable or pleasant things by chance. Example: Meeting my old friend at the airport was pure serendipity.Esoteric /藢蓻s蓹藞t蓻r瑟k/ (adj.): Intended for or understood by only a small number of people with specialized knowledge. Example: The professor gave an esoteric lecture on ancient philosophy.Cacophony /k忙藞k蓲f蓹ni/ (noun): A harsh, discordant mixture of sounds. Example: The traffic created a loud cacophony in the city.Sycophant /藞s瑟k蓹f忙nt/ (noun): A person who acts overly obedient or flattering to someone important to gain an advantage. Example: The manager was surrounded by sycophants who agreed with everything.Complex to Pronounce (Phonetic Triggers)Colonel /藞k蓽藧rn蓹l/: A high-ranking military officer (sounds exactly like "kernel").Worcestershire /藞w蕣st蓹r蕛蓹r/: A type of savory British sauce.Anemone /蓹藞n蓻m蓹ni/: A brightly colored sea creature or flower.Mischievous /藞m瑟st蕛瑟v蓹s/: Playful in a naughty or troublesome way.Complex to Spell (Orthographic Triggers)Connoisseur: An expert judge in matters of taste or fine art.Mnemonic: A system or pattern of letters/ideas to assist the memory.Conscientious: Governed by conscience; meticulous and careful.If you want to build your vocabulary further, tell me:Do you want more examples of these words?Should we focus on academic/formal terms?Do you need words for a specific exam (like SAT, GRE, or IELTS)?Here is the list of complex words provided as plain text for easy copying and pasting:Advanced Vocabulary (Complex Meanings)Ephemeral /蓹藞f蓻m蓹r蓹l/ (adj.): Lasting for a very short time. Example: The traffic created a loud cacophony in the city.Sycophant /藞s瑟k蓹f忙nt/ (noun): A person who acts overly obedient or flattering to someone important to gain an advantage. Example: The manager was surrounded by sycophants who agreed with everything.Complex to Pronounce (Phonetic Triggers)Colonel /藞k蓽藧rn蓹l/: A high-ranking military officer (sounds exactly like "kernel").Worcestershire /藞w蕣st蓹r蕛蓹r/: A type of savory British sauce.Anemone /蓹藞n蓻m蓹ni/: A brightly colored sea creature or flower.Mischievous /藞m瑟st蕛瑟v蓹s/: Playful in a naughty or troublesome way.Complex to Spell (Orthographic Triggers)Connoisseur: An expert judge in matters of taste or fine art.Mnemonic: A system or pattern of letters/ideas to assist the memory.Conscientious: Governed by conscience; meticulous and careful.If you want to build your vocabulary further, tell me:Do you want more examples of these words?Should we focus on academic/formal terms?Do you need words for a specific exam (like SAT, GRE, or IELTS)?Here is the list of complex words provided as plain text for easy copying and pasting:Advanced Vocabulary (Complex Meanings)Ephemeral /蓹藞f蓻m蓹r蓹l/ (adj.): Lasting for a very short time.
